id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMeredith2010539–542Sampson2011500_440-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeredith2010539–542Sampson2011500-440">[439]</a></sup> Mandela married his third wife, Graça Machel, on his 80th birthday in July 1998.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMeredith2010xvii,_576Sampson2011549–551_441-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeredith2010xvii,_576Sampson2011549–551-441">[440]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception_and_legacy">Reception and legacy</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nelson_Mandela_tributes_in_Parliament_Square_-_London_-_DSCF0404.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3072" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Nelson_Mandela_tributes_in_Parliament_Square_-_London_-_DSCF0404.jpg/220px-Nelson_Mandela_tributes_in_Parliament_Square_-_London_-_DSCF0404.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Nelson_Mandela_tributes_in_Parliament_Square_-_London_-_DSCF0404.jpg/330px-Nelson_Mandela_tributes_in_Parliament_Square_-_London_-_DSCF0404.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Nelson_Mandela_tributes_in_Parliament_Square_-_London_-_DSCF0404.jpg/440px-Nelson_Mandela_tributes_in_Parliament_Square_-_London_-_DSCF0404.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nelson_Mandela_tributes_in_Parliament_Square_-_London_-_DSCF0404.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Flowers left at the <a href="/wiki/Statue_of_Nelson_Mandela,_Parliament_Square" title="Statue of Nelson Mandela, Parliament Square">Mandela statue</a> in London's Parliament Square following his death</div></div></div>
<p>By the time of his death, within South Africa Mandela was widely considered both "the father of the nation"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-442"><a href="#cite_note-442">[441]</a></sup> and "the founding father of democracy".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMeredith2010565_443-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeredith2010565-443">[442]</a></sup> Outside of South Africa, he was a "global icon",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarnard20141,_2Ndlovu-Gatsheni2014906_444-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarnard20141,_2Ndlovu-Gatsheni2014906-444">[443]</a></sup> with the scholar of South African studies Rita Barnard describing him as "one of the most revered figures of our time".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarnard20141,_2_445-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarnard20141,_2-445">[444]</a></sup> One biographer considered him "a modern democratic hero".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELodge2006225_446-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELodge2006225-446">[445]</a></sup> Some have portrayed Mandela in messianic terms,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESuttner2007125–126_447-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESuttner2007125–126-447">[446]</a></sup> in contrast to his own statement that "I was not a messiah, but an ordinary man who had become a leader because of extraordinary circumstances."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMeredith2010599Barnard20144_448-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeredith2010599Barnard20144-448">[447]</a></sup> He is often cited alongside <a href="/wiki/Mahatma_Gandhi" title="Mahatma Gandhi">Mahatma Gandhi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther_King_Jr." title="Martin Luther King Jr.">Martin Luther King Jr.</a> as one of the 20th century's exemplary anti-racist and anti-colonial leaders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoehmer200882Ndlovu-Gatsheni2014918_449-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoehmer200882Ndlovu-Gatsheni2014918-449">[448]</a></sup> Boehmer described him as "a totem of the totemic values of our age: toleration and liberal democracy"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoehmer200816_450-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoehmer200816-450">[449]</a></sup> and "a universal symbol of social justice".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoehmer20081_451-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoehmer20081-451">[450]</a></sup>
</p><p>Mandela's international fame emerged during his incarceration in the 1980s, when he became the world's most famous <a href="/wiki/Political_prisoner" title="Political prisoner">political prisoner</a>, a symbol of the anti-apartheid cause, and an icon for millions who embraced the ideal of human equality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarnard20141_255-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarnard20141-255">[254]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-452"><a href="#cite_note-452">[451]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-453"><a href="#cite_note-453">[452]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-454"><a href="#cite_note-454">[453]</a></sup> In 1986, Mandela's biographer characterised him as "the embodiment of the struggle for liberation" in South Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBenson198613_455-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBenson198613-455">[454]</a></sup> Meredith stated that in becoming "a potent symbol of resistance" to apartheid during the 1980s, he had gained "mythical status" internationally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMeredith2010xv_456-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeredith2010xv-456">[455]</a></sup> Sampson commented that even during his life, this myth had become "so powerful that it blurs the realities", converting Mandela into "a secular saint".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESampson2011xxvi_457-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESampson2011xxvi-457">[456]</a></sup> Within a decade of the end of his presidency, Mandela's era was widely thought of as "a golden age of hope and harmony",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMeredith2010599_458-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeredith2010599-458">[457]</a></sup> with much <a href="/wiki/Nostalgia" title="Nostalgia">nostalgia</a> being expressed for it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFreund2014296_459-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFreund2014296-459">[458]</a></sup> His name was often invoked by those criticising his successors like Mbeki and Zuma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMangcu2013101_460-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMangcu2013101-460">[459]</a></sup> Across the world, Mandela earned international acclaim for his activism in overcoming apartheid and fostering racial reconciliation,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMeredith2010xvi_414-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeredith2010xvi-414">[413]</a></sup> coming to be viewed as "a moral authority" with a great "concern for truth".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESampson2011582_461-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESampson2011582-461">[460]</a></sup> Mandela's iconic status has been blamed for concealing the complexities of his life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESuttner201617_462-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESuttner201617-462">[461]</a></sup>
</p><p>Mandela generated controversy throughout his career as an activist and politician,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarnard20142_463-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarnard20142-463">[462]</a></sup> having detractors on both the right and the radical left.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoehmer2008173_464-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoehmer2008173-464">[463]</a></sup> During the 1980s, Mandela was widely labelled a terrorist by prominent political figures in the Western world for his embrace of political violence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoehmer200546_465-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoehmer200546-465">[464]</a></sup> According to Thatcher, for instance, the ANC was "a typical terrorist organisation".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESampson2011360_466-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESampson2011360-466">[465]</a></sup> The US government's <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">State</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">Defense</a> departments officially designated the ANC as a terrorist organisation, resulting in Mandela remaining on their terrorism watch-list until 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-467"><a href="#cite_note-467">[466]</a></sup> On the left, some voices in the ANC—among them <a href="/wiki/Frank_B._Wilderson_III" title="Frank B. Wilderson III">Frank B. Wilderson III</a>—accused him of <a href="/wiki/Selling_out" title="Selling out">selling out</a> for agreeing to enter negotiations with the apartheid government and for not implementing the reforms of the Freedom Charter during his presidency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarnard20142Ndlovu-Gatsheni2014918_468-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarnard20142Ndlovu-Gatsheni2014918-468">[467]</a></sup> According to Barnard, "there is also a sense in which his chiefly bearing and mode of conduct, the very respect and authority he accrued in representing his nation in his own person, went against the spirit of democracy",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarnard20142_463-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarnard20142-463">[462]</a></sup> and concerns were similarly expressed that he placed his own status and celebrity above the transformation of his country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENdlovu-Gatsheni2014918_469-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENdlovu-Gatsheni2014918-469">[468]</a></sup> His government would be criticised for its failure to deal with both the HIV/AIDS pandemic and the high levels of poverty in South Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarnard20142_463-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarnard20142-463">[462]</a></sup> Mandela was also criticised for his friendship with political leaders such as Castro, Gaddafi, and Suharto—deemed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dictators" title="Dictators">dictators</a> by critics—as well as his refusal to condemn their governments' human rights violations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-470"><a href="#cite_note-470">[469]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Orders.2C_decorations.2C_monuments.2C_and_honours"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Orders,_decorations,_monuments,_and_honours">Orders, decorations, monuments, and honours</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_honours_received_by_Nelson_Mandela" title="List of awards and honours received by Nelson Mandela">List of awards and honours received by Nelson Mandela</a></div>
<p>Over the course of his life, Mandela was given over 250 awards, accolades, prizes, honorary degrees and citizenships in recognition of his political achievements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CT12_471-0"><a href="#cite_note-CT12-471">[470]</a></sup>
Among his awards were the Nobel Peace Prize,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarber200468Lodge2006182Meredith2010494Sampson2011474_229-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarber200468Lodge2006182Meredith2010494Sampson2011474-229">[228]</a></sup> the US <a href="/wiki/Presidential_Medal_of_Freedom" title="Presidential Medal of Freedom">Presidential Medal of Freedom</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-472"><a href="#cite_note-472">[471]</a></sup> the Soviet Union's <a href="/wiki/Lenin_Peace_Prize" title="Lenin Peace Prize">Lenin Peace Prize</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CT12_471-1"><a href="#cite_note-CT12-471">[470]</a></sup> and the Libyan <a href="/wiki/Al-Gaddafi_International_Prize_for_Human_Rights" title="Al-Gaddafi International Prize for Human Rights">Al-Gaddafi International Prize for Human Rights</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TimeGadafiPrize_473-0"><a href="#cite_note-TimeGadafiPrize-473">[472]</a></sup> In 1990, India awarded him the <a href="/wiki/Bharat_Ratna" title="Bharat Ratna">Bharat Ratna</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-474"><a href="#cite_note-474">[473]</a></sup> and in 1992 Pakistan gave him their <a href="/wiki/Nishan-e-Pakistan" title="Nishan-e-Pakistan">Nishan-e-Pakistan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-475"><a href="#cite_note-475">[474]</a></sup> The same year, he was awarded the Atatürk Peace Award by Turkey; he at first refused the award, citing human rights violations committed by Turkey at the time,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ataturk_476-0"><a href="#cite_note-ataturk-476">[475]</a></sup> but later accepted the award in 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CT12_471-2"><a href="#cite_note-CT12-471">[470]</a></sup> He was given the Fulbright Prize for International Understanding by the <a href="/wiki/Fulbright_Association" title="Fulbright Association">Fulbright Association</a> in 1993. He was appointed to the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Isabella_the_Catholic" title="Order of Isabella the Catholic">Order of Isabella the Catholic</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-477"><a href="#cite_note-477">[476]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Canada" title="Order of Canada">Order of Canada</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-478"><a href="#cite_note-478">[477]</a></sup> and was the first living person to be made an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Honorary_Citizenship_of_Canada" title="Honorary Citizenship of Canada">honorary Canadian citizen</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-479"><a href="#cite_note-479">[478]</a></sup> Queen Elizabeth II appointed him as a Bailiff Grand Cross of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Saint_John_(chartered_1888)" title="Order of Saint John (chartered 1888)">Order of St. John</a> and granted him membership in the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Merit" title="Order of Merit">Order of Merit</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-480"><a href="#cite_note-480">[479]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2004, Johannesburg granted Mandela the <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_the_City" title="Freedom of the City">Freedom of the City</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-481"><a href="#cite_note-481">[480]</a></sup> and in 2008 a Mandela statue was unveiled at the spot where Mandela was released from prison.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-482"><a href="#cite_note-482">[481]</a></sup> On the <a href="/wiki/Day_of_Reconciliation" title="Day of Reconciliation">Day of Reconciliation</a> 2013, a bronze statue of Mandela was unveiled at Pretoria's Union Buildings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-483"><a href="#cite_note-483">[482]</a></sup>
In November 2009, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a> proclaimed Mandela's birthday, 18 July, as "<a href="/wiki/Mandela_Day" title="Mandela Day">Mandela Day</a>", marking his contribution to the anti-apartheid struggle. It called on individuals to donate 67 minutes to doing something for others, commemorating the 67 years that Mandela had been a part of the movement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-484"><a href="#cite_note-484">[483]</a></sup> In 2015 the UN General Assembly named the amended <a href="/wiki/Standard_Minimum_Rules_for_the_Treatment_of_Prisoners" title="Standard Minimum Rules for the Treatment of Prisoners">Standard Minimum Rules for the Treatment of Prisoners</a> as "the Mandela Rules" to honour his legacy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-485"><a href="#cite_note-485">[484]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biographies_and_popular_media">Biographies and popular media</span></h3>
<p>The first biography of Mandela was authored by <a href="/wiki/Mary_Benson_(campaigner)" title="Mary Benson (campaigner)">Mary Benson</a>, based on brief interviews with him that she had conducted in the 1960s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELodge20068_486-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELodge20068-486">[485]</a></sup> Two authorised biographies were later produced by friends of Mandela.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELodge2006vii_487-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELodge2006vii-487">[486]</a></sup> The first was Fatima Meer's <i>Higher Than Hope</i>, which was heavily influenced by Winnie and thus placed great emphasis on Mandela's family.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELodge2006vii,_13–14_488-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELodge2006vii,_13–14-488">[487]</a></sup> The second was Anthony Sampson's <i>Mandela</i>, published in 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELodge2006vii_487-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELodge2006vii-487">[486]</a></sup> Other biographies included Martin Meredith's <i>Mandela</i>, first published in 1997, and Tom Lodge's <i>Mandela</i>, brought out in 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELodge2006vii_487-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELodge2006vii-487">[486]</a></sup>
</p><p>Since the late 1980s, Mandela's image began to appear on a proliferation of items, among them "photographs, paintings, drawings, statues, public murals, buttons, t-shirts, refrigerator magnets, and more",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENelson2014130_364-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENelson2014130-364">[363]</a></sup> items that have been characterised as "Mandela kitsch".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENelson2014138_489-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENelson2014138-489">[488]</a></sup> In the 1980s he was the subject of several songs, such as <a href="/wiki/The_Specials" title="The Specials">The Specials</a>' "<a href="/wiki/Free_Nelson_Mandela" title="Free Nelson Mandela">Free Nelson Mandela</a>", <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Masekela" title="Hugh Masekela">Hugh Masekela</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Bring_Him_Back_Home_(Nelson_Mandela)" title="Bring Him Back Home (Nelson Mandela)">Bring Him Back Home (Nelson Mandela)</a>", and <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Clegg" title="Johnny Clegg">Johnny Clegg</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Asimbonanga" title="Asimbonanga">Asimbonanga (Mandela)</a>", which helped to bring awareness of his imprisonment to an international audience.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-490"><a href="#cite_note-490">[489]</a></sup>
</p><p>Following his death, many <a href="/wiki/Internet_meme" title="Internet meme">internet memes</a> appeared featuring images of Mandela with his inspirational quotes superimposed onto them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENelson2014130_364-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENelson2014130-364">[363]</a></sup> Mandela has also been depicted in films on multiple occasions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBromley201441_491-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBromley201441-491">[490]</a></sup> Some of these, such as the 2013 feature film <i><a href="/wiki/Mandela:_Long_Walk_to_Freedom" title="Mandela: Long Walk to Freedom">Mandela: Long Walk to Freedom</a></i>, the 2017 miniseries <i><a href="/wiki/Madiba_(miniseries)" title="Madiba (miniseries)">Madiba</a></i> and the 1996 documentary <i>Mandela</i>, have focused on covering his adult life in entirety or until his inaugural as president others, such as the 2009 feature film <i><a href="/wiki/Invictus_(film)" title="Invictus (film)">Invictus</a></i> and the 2010 documentary <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_16th_Man" title="The 16th Man">The 16th Man</a></i>, have focused on specific events in his life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBromley201441_491-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBromley201441-491">[490]</a></sup> It has been argued that in <i>Invictus</i> and other films, "the America film industry" has played a significant part in "the crafting of Mandela's global image".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELukhele2012289_492-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELukhele2012289-492">[491]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_peace_activists" title="List of peace activists">List of peace activists</a></li></ul>

<li id="cite_note-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-4">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Mandela used the spelling Rolihlahla; see for example <a class="external text" href="http://www.mandela.gov.za/" rel="nofollow">official website</a>. <a href="/wiki/Peter_Mtuze" title="Peter Mtuze">Peter Mtuze</a> notes that the orthography of <a href="/wiki/Xhosa_language" title="Xhosa language">Xhosa</a> names has changed since the time of Mandela's schooling, and that it would now be written Rholihlahla.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></span>
</li>

<ul><li>1981: <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_L%C3%B3pez_Portillo" title="José López Portillo">José López Portillo</a></li>
<li>1982: <a href="/wiki/Enrique_V._Iglesias" title="Enrique V. Iglesias">Enrique V. Iglesias</a></li>

</div></td></tr><tr><th class="navbox-group" scope="row" style="background:#addeff;;width:1%">1990s</th><td class="navbox-list-with-group navbox-list navbox-even" style="width:100%;padding:0"><div style="padding:0 0.25em">
